## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and current population P. This is a classic population dynamics problem where the growth rate depends on population size through various density-dependent and density-independent mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- {'name': 'Exponential (Malthusian) growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P', 'scenario': 'Density-independent growth where rate is proportional to population size'}
- {'name': 'Logistic growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with carrying capacity, the most common population model'}
- {'name': 'Gompertz growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate decreases logarithmically as population approaches carrying capacity'}
- {'name': 'Theta-logistic model', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)', 'scenario': 'Generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence controlled by exponent'}
- {'name': 'Allee effect model', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P)', 'scenario': 'Population growth with strong Allee effect (minimum viable population threshold)'}
- {'name': 'Richards growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2', 'scenario': 'Flexible asymmetric sigmoidal growth model generalizing logistic'}
- {'name': 'Beverton-Holt continuous analog', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)', 'scenario': 'Density-dependent growth with hyperbolic saturation in per-capita rate'}
- {'name': 'Power-law density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1', 'scenario': 'Growth rate as a power function of population size'}
- {'name': 'Time-varying exponential growth', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t)', 'scenario': 'Growth rate with time-dependent environmental change'}
- {'name': 'Logistic with time-varying capacity', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t))', 'scenario': 'Logistic growth where carrying capacity changes over time'}
- {'name': 'Von Bertalanffy-type growth rate', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P', 'scenario': 'Balance between anabolic (power-law) and catabolic (linear) processes'}
- {'name': 'Quadratic density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2', 'scenario': 'Linear plus quadratic terms representing intrinsic growth and crowding'}
- {'name': 'Polynomial density dependence', 'formula': 'dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3', 'scenario': 'Higher-order density effects including cubic terms for complex dynamics'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent regulation → multiplicative factor (1 - P/K) or (1 - c*P) reducing growth at high population
- Allee effects (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P - c) introducing a lower threshold
- Per-capita growth rate declining with P → dP_dt/P is a decreasing function of P, suggesting rational or logarithmic forms in P
- Logarithmic feedback → log(K/P) or log(c/P) terms indicate Gompertz-type asymmetric growth dynamics
- Competing anabolic vs catabolic scaling → difference of power laws P^a - c*P^b with different exponents models metabolic scaling in growth
- Time-explicit dependence → multiplicative exp(c*t) or polynomial in t modulating growth indicates non-stationary environmental conditions
- Cubic population terms → P*(P-a)*(K-P) structure indicates bistability or strong Allee effects with two stable equilibria
- Ratio of population polynomials → rational functions like P/(1+c*P) indicate resource competition or interference effects

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate.

## GT Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
0.17*(−1 + P/1.047)*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − P/10.21)*P + 0.17*(1 − exp(−0.097*P))*P
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote a = 0.17, b = 1.047, d = 10.21, k = 0.097.

**Term 1:** a*(−1 + P/b)*(1 − P/d)*P = a*(P/b − 1)*(1 − P/d)*P

**Term 2:** a*(1 − P/d)*P

**Term 3:** a*(1 − exp(−k*P))*P

Combine Terms 1 and 2:
a*(1 − P/d)*P * [(P/b − 1) + 1] = a*(1 − P/d)*P * (P/b) = a*P²/b * (1 − P/d)

So Terms 1+2 = a*P²/b − a*P³/(b*d)

Term 3 = a*P − a*P*exp(−k*P)

**Total GT = a*P²/b − a*P³/(b*d) + a*P − a*P*exp(−k*P)**

With numerical values:
- Coefficient of P³: −a/(b*d) ≈ −0.17/(1.047*10.21) ≈ −0.0159
- Coefficient of P²: a/b ≈ 0.17/1.047 ≈ 0.1623
- Coefficient of P: a ≈ 0.17
- Exponential term: −a*P*exp(−k*P) = −0.17*P*exp(−0.097*P)

So **GT = c_3*P³ + c_2*P² + c_1*P + c_exp*P*exp(−k*P)** where the exponential term is essential.

The GT has these basis functions: P³, P², P, P*exp(−kP).

Now let me check each candidate for structural compatibility.

### Candidate 1:
`(P*c0*(P + c1) + P*(P²*c2 + P*c3 + c4) + P^c5*c6*(P + c1))/(P + c1)`

= P*c0 + P*(P²*c2 + P*c3 + c4)/(P+c1) + c6*P^c5

The polynomial fraction doesn't simplify to give an exponential. This has P^c5 (power law) instead of P*exp(−kP). These are different basis functions.

**But wait** - can P^c5 match P*exp(−kP)? No, power laws and exponentials are fundamentally different functions.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]
